lspace="0em" rspace="2em">⁣</mo><mi>τ</mi><mo>≪</mo><mfrac><msup><mrow><mi>L</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></msub></mfrac></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div>where τ is the time duration of the current pulse, <i>m</i><sub>B</sub> the mass loading of the active material, <i>V</i><sub>M</sub> the molar volume of the electrode material, <i>M</i><sub>B</sub> the molar mass of the electrode, <i>S</i> the area of the electrode–electrolyte interface, Δ<i>E</i><sub>S</sub> the steady-state voltage change between before and after the current pulse, and Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> the voltage change during the current pulse. During the sodiation process, CK anode delivers superior <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> in DEGDME-based electrolytes than EC/DEC-based electrolytes, and it offers preferable <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values than the C anode in DEGDME-based electrolytes (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>b). During the desodiation process, the CK anode has comparable <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values in DEGDME- and EC/DEC-based electrolytes, and it possesses better <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values than the C anode in DEGDME-based electrolytes (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>c). The comparison of <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> between the C and CK anodes is in accordance with the results of the mentioned CV analysis. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>d shows the Nyquist plots of all anodes from the EIS test to investigate the transportation of Na<sup>+</sup> in two electrolytes. The <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (charge-transfer resistance) values are 14.3, 8.2, and 1022 Ω of C-DEGDME, CK-DEGDME, and CK-EC/DEC, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/suppl_file/am4c03425_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S6</a>). Besides, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> involves the desolvation of Na<sup>+</sup>; thus, the larger the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> is, the higher the desolvation energy is, and the more sluggish the kinetics is. The σ-values of C-DEGDME, CK-DEGDME, and CK-EC/DEC, from the slope of the plot of Z′ vs ω<sup>–1/2</sup>, are 21.69, 11.16, and 134.85, respectively (see <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/suppl_file/am4c03425_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S16</a>). Based on the mentioned σ values, the following equation is observed: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref32 ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref32 ref48" aria-label="reference 9, 32 and 48">(9,32,48)</a><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-84"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-85"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-86"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-87"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-88"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-89" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-90">D</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-91" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-92"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-93" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-94">Na</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-95" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-96">+</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-97"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-98" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-99"><span class="MJXp-mfrac" id="MJXp-Span-100" style="vertical-align: 0.25em;"><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-101"><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-102"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-103" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-104">R</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-105" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-106">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-107"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-108" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-109">T</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-110" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-111">2</span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-box" style="margin-top: -0.9em;"><span class="MJXp-denom"><span><span class="MJXp-rule" style="height: 1em; border-top: none; border-bottom: 1px solid; margin: 0.1em 0px;"></span></span><span><span class="MJXp-box"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-112"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-113">2</span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-114"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-115" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-116">A</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-117" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-118">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-119"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-120" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-121">n</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-122" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-123">4</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-124"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-125" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-126">F</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-127" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-128">4</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-129"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-130" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-131">C</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-132" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-133">2</span></span></span><span class="MJXp-msup" id="MJXp-Span-134"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-135" style="margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-136">σ</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-137" style="vertical-align: 0.5em;"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-138">2</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-2"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>R</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>T</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><msup><mrow><mi>A</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>n</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>F</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>C</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mi>σ</mi></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mrow></mfrac></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div>where <i>R</i> is the gas constant, <i>T</i> represents absolute temperature, <i>n</i> is the number of electrons transferred during the reaction, <i>A</i> is the electrode active area, <i>F</i> is the Faraday constant, <i>C</i> is the Na<sup>+</sup> phase density, and σ is the slope representing the relationship between <i>Z</i>′ and ω<sup>–1/2</sup>. The obtained <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values of C-DEGDME, CK-DEGDME, and CK-EC/DEC are 1.22 × 10<sup>–10</sup>, 4.61 × 10<sup>–10</sup>, and 3.16 × 10<sup>–12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. All the GITT and EIS analyses indicate that the CK anode has superior <i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub> values in DEGDME-based electrolyte due to the special structure of carbon and fast Na<sup>+</sup> dynamic behavior in ether electrolytes.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/medium/am4c03425_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/large/am4c03425_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Kinetics analysis of the C and CK anodes in DEGDME- or EC/DEC-based SIB half-cells. (a) GITT potential profiles with a pulse current of 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> for 0.5 h, followed by a 1 h relaxation process. (b, c) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients calculated from the GITT potential profiles for discharge processes (panel (b)) and charge processes (panel (c)). (d) Nyquist plots. (e) <i>b</i>-value calculation. (f) Capacitive contributions at different scan rates. (g) Schematic illustration of the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of the CK anode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/large/am4c03425_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c03425&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">CV curves, shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/suppl_file/am4c03425_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S17</a>, manifest the Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption at ultramicropores from the redox peaks below 1 V, as well as the Na<sup>+</sup> physisorption (chemisorption)/desorption from the rectangle-like shape over 1 V, caused by open pores (oxygen doping). Based on the CV curves from 0.2 to 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, the type of the capacity for CK anode is identified by using the equation <i>i</i> = <i>av</i><sup><i>b</i></sup> (for <i>b</i>-values near 0.5/1.0─diffusion-controlled capacity (sluggish)/ capacitive-controlled capacity (fast)). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref48 ref53" aria-label="reference 48 and 53">(48,53)</a> By fitting the peak current under different scanning rates, the <i>b</i>-values are higher and close to 1.0 for the CK anode in DEGDME-based electrolytes, in contrast to others (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>e), which also demonstrates the benefits of structure and electrolyte. The proportion of capacitive/diffusion contribution for all anodes in two electrolytes is calculated by using the equation <i>i</i>(<i>V</i>) = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> (capacitive contribution) <i>+ k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>0.5</sup> (diffusion contribution). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50 ref51" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50 ref51" aria-label="reference 50 and 51">(50,51)</a> According to this equation, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/suppl_file/am4c03425_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S17</a> exhibits the obtained capacitive contribution at 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> of 63.7% (blue shadow) for the CK anode in EC/DEC-based electrolytes, which is poorer than that observed for the C and CK anode (94.8% and 95.6%, respectively) (blue shadowing) in DEGDME-based electrolytes. Furthermore, from 0.2 to 1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, the capacitive contribution of CK anode delivers the maximum value in DEGDME-based electrolyte (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>f), manifesting the lotus-root-like framework and DEGDME-based electrolytes can make a synergistic effect to improve Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics, wherein DEGDME-based electrolytes play a dominant role because of their lower desolvation energy.</div><div class="NLM_p last">To sum up, there are three main reasons for the outstanding Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of CK anode in DEGDME-based electrolyte (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>g):<table class="listgroup" border="0" width="95%" list-type="label"><tbody><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(1)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">Considering the structure of CK anode, the lotus-root-like framework can facilitate Na<sup>+</sup> transportation, and there are plentiful pores that can accommodate volume change for high stability.</p></td></tr><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(2)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">The high ocygen-doping level can increase the wettability with electrolyte, defects/disorder for adsorbing Na<sup>+</sup>, and redox reactions, such as C═O + Na<sup>+</sup> + e<sup>–</sup> ↔ C–O–Na. Meanwhile, the high oxygen content enlarges interlayer spacing and provides active sites for Na<sup>+</sup> insertion.</p></td></tr><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(3)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">Considering the DEGDME-based electrolyte, it can provide easy desolvated Na<sup>+</sup>, preferable capacitive contribution, high <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values, and a thinner NaF-based SEI layer with poor interface impedance, leading to superior Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics, which dominates the high-rate performance of SIBs.</p></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i15">4.  Conclusion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, an O-doped porous carbon (CK) is obtained by the strategy of biomimetic-mineralization-assisted self-activation, which favors the formation of a uniform precursor, lotus-root-like carbon framework, and structural disorder with abundant defects. Based on the advantages of structure and oxygen doping for CK, and Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics for ether-based electrolyte, the as-prepared CK anode delivers high ICE (82.9%) and excellent storage capability (485.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup>). Assembled with Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode, the NVP//CK full-cell achieves a high energy density of 204.4 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> in ether-based electrolytes. Both sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) half-cell and full-cell tests show the splendid Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of CK anode, accompanied by following factors, proved by ex-situ characterizations and electrochemical kinetics tests:<table class="listgroup" border="0" width="95%" list-type="label"><tbody><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(1)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">The lotus-root-like framework, hierarchical pores, and high degree of oxygen doping suit Na<sup>+</sup> storage but with limited improvement of Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics.</p></td></tr><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(2)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">The composition of the SEI layer influences Na<sup>+</sup> storage to a certain degree, notably the high concentration of NaF, which possesses a low diffusion activation energy.</p></td></tr><tr class="li1"><td valign="top">(3)</td><td colspan="5" valign="top" class="paragraph"><p class="last">Ether-based electrolytes have better electrochemical kinetics than ester-based electrolytes, which determines the electrochemical performance.</p></td></tr></tbody></table>All of the above results indicate the excellence of our synthesis strategy and ester-based electrolytes, prompting an increasing concern regarding the development of porous carbon anode and ether electrolyte-based electrochemical energy storage. The work provides a systematic understanding for achieving next-generation sustainable SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="dataAvailabilityNotesSection"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="dataAvailabilityNotesSection">Data Availability</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">Data will be made available on request.</p></div><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i17">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c03425?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c03425</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">SEM images;                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine SnSSe/multilayer graphene nanosheet nanocomposite as a high-performance anode material for potassium-ion half/full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Zuyue; Xu, Jingyi; Xu, Zhenhua; Zhang, Min; He, Yanan; Bao, Jianchun; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">60</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">241-248</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layer-structured SnSSe attracts much attention as an anode material for potassium storage due to its large theor. capacity.  Unfortunately, their practical application is severely restrained by the dramatic volumetric variation of SnSSe.  Herein, we synthesize ultrafine SnSSe/multilayer graphene nanosheet (SnSSe/MGS) by a vacuum solid-phase reaction and subsequent ball milling.  Owing to the strong synergistic effect between the two components, the obtained SnSSe/MGS nanocomposite exhibits a high reversible capacity (423 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1), excellent rate property (218 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and stable cycling performance (271 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at 100 mA g-1) in potassium-ion half batteries.  Moreover, the full cell assembled by the SnSSe/MGS anode and the potassiated 3,4,9,10-perylene-tetracarboxylic aciddianhydride cathode shows excellent electrochem. performance between 0.2 and 3.3 V (209 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 100 cycles).  The presented two-step synthesis strategy of SnSSe/MGS may also provide ideas to craft other alloy-type anode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref8" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.0c02327"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Water Chestnut-Derived Slope-Dominated Carbon as a High-Performance Anode for High-Safety Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">11410</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">11417</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsaem.0c02327</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D11410-11417%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26issue%3D11%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DS.%2BDu%26author%3DZ.%2BYi%26author%3DJ.%2BHan%26author%3DC.%2BLai%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26title%3DWater%2BChestnut-Derived%2BSlope-Dominated%2BCarbon%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Performance%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BHigh-Safety%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsaem.0c02327&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsaem.0c02327&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Water Chestnut-Derived Slope-Dominated Carbon as a High-Performance Anode for High-Safety Potassium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Zhenhua; Du, Shuangli; Yi, Zuyue; Han, Jingchen; Lai, Chenling; Xu, Yifan; Zhou, Xiaosi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11410-11417</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0962</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The overall electrochem. performance of carbon anodes for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) is considerably restricted by their poor cyclic property and rate capability issues.  Herein, we report a water chestnut-derived slope-dominated carbon anode through moderate-temp. pyrolysis at 900°C, which manifests a high initial reversible capacity of 253.2 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, remarkable rate property of 134.8 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1, and impressive cycling performance of 220.5 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles.  When assembled with the potassiated 3,4,9,10-perylene-tetracarboxylic acid dianhydride cathode, the initial reversible capacity reaches 124.3 mAh g-1 at 25 mA g-1, and 84.7% of the capacity is maintained even after 300 cycles at 50 mA g-1.  The improved potassium storage properties could be ascribed to the disordered microstructure with relatively larger oxygen-contg. defect concn., high sp. surface area, and stochastically oriented short graphene nanosheets.  D. functional theory calcns. illustrate that oxygen doping can effectively alter the charge d. distribution of carbon and facilitate the adsorption of K+ on water chestnut-derived carbon, which boosts potassium ion storage.  This work would provide a promising avenue to design and synthesize slope-dominated carbon materials for low-cost PIBs with excellent rate and cycling properties and high safety.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref9" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202207751"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Terrones, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Combustion Activation Induced Solid-State Synthesis for N, B Co-Doped Carbon/Zinc Borate Anode with a Boosting of Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A revised mechanistic model for sodium insertion in hard carbons</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Au, Heather; Alptekin, Hande; Jensen, Anders C. S.; Olsson, Emilia; O'Keefe, Christopher A.; Smith, Thomas; Crespo-Ribadeneyra, Maria; Headen, Thomas F.; Grey, Clare P.; Cai, Qiong; Drew, Alan J.; Titirici, Maria-Magdalena</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3469-3479</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons have shown considerable promise as anodes for emerging sodium-ion battery technologies.  Current understanding of sodium-storage behavior in hard carbons attributes capacity to filling of graphitic interlayers and pores, and adsorption at defects, although there is still considerable debate regarding the voltages at which these mechanisms occur.  Here, ex situ23Na solid-state NMR and total scattering studies on a systematically tuned series of hard carbons revealed the formation of increasingly metallic sodium clusters in direct correlation to the growing pore size, occurring only in samples which exhibited a low voltage plateau.  Combining exptl. results with DFT calcns., we propose a revised mechanistic model in which sodium ions store first simultaneously and continuously at defects, within interlayers and on pore surfaces.  Once these higher energy binding sites are filled, pore filling occurs during the plateau region, where the densely confined sodium takes on a greater degree of metallicity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding of the Sodium Storage Mechanism in Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Carbon Energy.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1133</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1150</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in hard carbon anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xiaoyang; Liu, Changyu; Fang, Yongjin; Ai, Xinping; Zhong, Faping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbon has been regarded as the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its low cost, high reversible capacity, and low working potential.  However, the uncertain sodium storage mechanism hinders the rational design and synthesis of high-performance hard carbon anode materials for practical SIBs.  During the past decades, tremendous efforts have been put to stimulate the development of hard carbon materials.  In this review, we discuss the recent progress of the study on the sodium storage mechanism of hard carbon anodes, and the effective strategies to improve their sodium storage performance have been summarized.  It is anticipated that hard carbon anodes with high electrochem. properties will be inspired and fabricated for large-scale energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.2210203119"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Step-By-Step Desolvation Enables High-Rate And Ultra-Stable Sodium Storage in Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Proc.                 10.1002/adma.202008810</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D33%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D2008810%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D36%26author%3DR.%2BDong%26author%3DL.%2BZheng%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DQ.%2BNi%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DH.%2BRen%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DElucidating%2Bthe%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BFast%2BNa%2BStorage%2BKinetics%2Bin%2BEther%2BElectrolytes%2Bfor%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202008810&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202008810&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Elucidating the Mechanism of Fast Na Storage Kinetics in Ether Electrolytes for Hard Carbon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Ruiqi; Zheng, Lumin; Bai, Ying; Ni, Qiao; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng; Ren, Haixia; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">33</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">36</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2008810</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium storage performance of a hard carbon (HC) anode in ether electrolytes exhibits a higher initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) and better rate performance compared to conventional ester electrolytes.  However, the mechanism behind faster Na storage kinetics for HC in ether electrolytes remains unclear.  Herein, a unique solvated Na+ and Na+ co-intercalation mechanism in ether electrolytes is reported using designed monodispersed HC nanospheres.  In addn., a thin solid electrolyte interphase film with a high inorg. proportion formed in an ether electrolyte is visualized by cryo transmission electron microscopy and depth-profiling XPS, which facilitates Na+ transportation, and results in a high ICE.  Furthermore, the fast solvated Na+ diffusion kinetics in ether electrolytes are also revealed via mol. dynamics simulation.  Owing to the contribution of the ether electrolytes, an excellent rate performance (214 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 with an ultrahigh plateau capacity of 120 mAh g-1) and a high ICE (84.93% at 1 A g-1) are obsd. in a half cell; in a full cell, an attractive specific capacity of 110.3 mAh g-1 is achieved after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.10.049"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailored Edge-Heteroatom Tri-Doping Strategy of Turbostratic Carbon Anodes for High-Rate Performance Lithium and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>54</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">498</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">507</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Ultramicroporous Carbon with Abundant C=O as Extended "Slope-Dominated" Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Wenlong; Hu, Fangyuan; Zhang, Tianpeng; Liu, Siyang; Song, Ce; Li, Nan; Weng, Zhihuan; Wang, Jinyan; Jian, Xigao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Sustainable Chemistry &amp; Engineering</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9727-9739</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASCECG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2168-0485</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The overall performance of carbon-based materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is still restricted by the sluggish transfer kinetics of Na+ and limited rate capability.  Specifically, introducing ultramicropores (pores width &lt;0.7 nm) into carbon materials may be effective in improving the anode performance of SIBs.  However, due to the difficulty of their synthesis and homogeneity regulation, ultramicroporous carbon as advanced SIB anodes as well as their sodium storage mechanisms have seldom been investigated.  Herein, carbon spheres with centralized ultramicropores and abundant C=O is facilely obtained by combining the in situ ion activation and the novel quant. air-assisted carbonization process for the first time.  The quant. air acts not only as a mild agent to activate the materials, but also as an oxygen dopant for forming oxygen-contg. functional groups.  As the optimized anode, quant. air-assisted carbonized spheres with a precursor wt. of 0.3 g (QACS-0.3) delivers a high rate capability (265 and 121 mAh g-1 at 0.05 and 5.0 A g-1, resp.) and good cycling stability (126 mAh g-1 after 5000 cycles at 5.0 A g-1).  Kinetic anal., theor. calcn., and ex situ testing technologies reveal that the ultramicropores can facilitate the diffusion of Na+ below 0.2 V; the synergistic effect of defects, C=O, and ultramicropores can extend the discharge curves and effectively improve the adsorption capacity of carbon materials.  Addnl., a new discharge model is proposed to explain the sodium storage behaviors in these electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202100808"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Egun, I.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis Strategies of Porous Carbon for Supercapacitor Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Jian; Zhang, Wenli; Alhebshi, Nuha A.; Salah, Numan; Alshareef, Husam N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small Methods</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Supercapacitors (SCs) have experienced a significant increase in research activity and commercialization during the past few decades.  As the primary and most important electrode active material for com. SCs, porous carbon is produced at an industrial-scale through traditional carbonization-activation strategies.  Nevertheless, com. porous carbon materials have some disadvantages such as high prodn. cost, corrosion of equipment, and emission of toxic gases and byproduct pollutants during prodn.  In recent years, huge efforts have been made to develop novel synthesis strategies for porous carbon materials.  This review focuses on the pore formation mechanisms in traditional carbonization-activation methods, emerging activation methods, template methods, self-template methods, and novel emerging methods for the synthesis of porous carbons for SCs.  Strategies developed so far for the synthesis of porous carbon materials are summarized.  The mechanisms and recent advances for each strategy are reviewed.  Furthermore, future directions and synthesis strategies for porous carbons are proposed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.apmate.2021.11.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Template-Assisted Synthesis of Porous Carbons for Supercapacitors</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced bio-inspired structural materials: Local properties determine overall performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Binjie; Han, Qigang; Zhang, Junqiu; Han, Zhiwu; Niu, Shichao; Ren, Luquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">41</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">177-199</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Natural materials have always attracted intensive attention from multidisciplinary scientists all over the world.  In fact, the ingenious and reasonable synthetic strategies of the limited components can always make natural materials achieve a superior performance that is far beyond their own.  Meanwhile, the local properties can det. the overall performance through regulating multiple characteristics, including structure, compn., and interface.  Living organisms can inspire the fabrication of artificial materials, which provides a clear vision for advanced materials research.  Therefore, inspired by this strategy, biomimetic structural materials are used to meet the strict and even extreme requirements of engineering materials.  In this review, we mainly clarify the difference of local properties in natural materials and explain how living organisms utilize very limited elements and compds. to control the local properties and further realize some specific function to adapt to the specific requirement of the environment.  In addn., the manufg. technologies and strategies common to bio-inspired structural materials are summarized.  Finally, a summary and prospects on the limitations of current techniques and the direction of future developments for the design of novel bio-inspired materials are given.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.34133/research.0164"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ping, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Bioinspired Additive Manufacturing of Hierarchical Materials: From Biostructures to Functions</span>. <i>Research</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">0164</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ether-based electrolytes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Liu, Mingquan; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4484-4536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202209523"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unraveling the Mechanism of Different Kinetics Performance Between Ether and Carbonate Ester Electrolytes in Hard Carbon Electrode</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">48</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2209523</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202209523</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D32%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2209523%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D48%26author%3DX.%2BYi%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BZhong%26author%3DS.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BGuo%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DG.%2BYan%26title%3DUnraveling%2Bthe%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BDifferent%2BKinetics%2BPerformance%2BBetween%2BEther%2Band%2BCarbonate%2BEster%2BElectrolytes%2Bin%2BHard%2BCarbon%2BElectrode%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.202209523&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.202209523&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling mechanism of different kinetics performance between ether and carbonate ester electrolytes in hard carbon electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Xiaoli; Li, Xinhai; Zhong, Jing; Wang, Siwu; Wang, Zhixing; Guo, Huajun; Wang, Jiexi; Yan, Guochun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2209523</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether electrolytes exhibit better rate kinetics than carbonate ester electrolytes when used in several kinds of anode materials, esp. in hard carbon (HC) for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the mechanism causing the remarkable kinetics difference is still unclear.  Here, a three-electrode system is used first to eliminate the influence of polarization from the Na counter electrode.  Then, there is systematic exploration from three steps of the electrode reaction process (Na+) storage in HC; de-solvation; Na+ migration through solid electrolyte interphase (SE), and the underlying mysteries are uncovered.  For Na+ storage in the bulk of the HC, it is found that two systems show the same storage mechanism and Na metallic nanoparticles will appear when discharged to 0.1 V.  In addn., faster de-solvation of the ether electrolyte is uncovered by three-electrode temp.-dependent EIS and solvation free energies calcn.  Moreover, the difference of the SEI layers is unraveled by XPS etching, SEM, and differential electrochem. mass spectrometry.  Most importantly, by discriminating the impacts of the SEI layers and de-solvation behavior, it can be concluded that the de-solvation process is the rate-controlling step of the electrode reaction process and is the main factor causing the kinetics differences between the two electrolytes.  The research provides a clear mechanism to illuminate fast kinetics for ether electrolytes, which will promote its application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA00845E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting the Ultrahigh Initial Coulombic Efficiency of Porous Carbon Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries Via in Situ Fabrication of a Passivation Interface</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">17</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">10780</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10788</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1TA00845E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D10780-10788%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26issue%3D17%26author%3DM.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DBoosting%2Bthe%2BUltrahigh%2BInitial%2BCoulombic%2BEfficiency%2Bof%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2BVia%2Bin%2BSitu%2BFabrication%2Bof%2Ba%2BPassivation%2BInterface%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD1TA00845E&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD1TA00845E&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting the ultrahigh initial coulombic efficiency of porous carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries via in situ fabrication of a passivation interface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Minghao; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng; Wang, Zhaohua; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10780-10788</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous carbon materials are regarded as one of the most promising candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their fast sodium storage performance.  However, the inadequate initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) resulting from the large sp. surface area still hinders the commercialization of porous carbon anodes.  Thus, it is important to synthesize porous carbon anodes with high electrochem. performance and improved ICE.  Here we prep. a nitrogen and oxygen rich porous carbon material (NOPC) and construct a uniform passivation layer using a sodium CM-cellulose (CMC) binder on the surface of the NOPC material.  The uniform passivation layer effectively deactivates the functional groups and suppresses the decompn. of electrolytes, resulting in an excellent ICE of 90%, which is ultrahigh and competitive among the reported carbon-based anodes in SIBs.  Specifically, the as-prepd. porous carbon anode delivers a reversible capacity of 191.7 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 90%.  This work suggests a general method to improve the ICE of a carbon material and hopefully facilitates the commercialization process of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202100538"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mathur, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vitreum Etching Assisted Fabrication of Porous Hollow Carbon Architectures for Enhanced Capacitive Sodium and Potassium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">25</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2100538</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile self-templating synthesis of layered carbon with N, S dual doping for highly efficient sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jiabao; Ding, Zibiao; Pan, Likun; Li, Jinliang; Wang, Chengyin; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen and sulfur co-doping is emerging as a promising approach to prominently improve the sodium storage performance of carbonaceous materials.  However, poisonous chems. and rigorous conditions are normally involved in their prepn., esp. in the sulfidation process.  Therefore, developing novel, facile and eco-friendly approaches to construct nitrogen and sulfur co-doped carbon (NSC) is still challenging.  In this work, a facile self-templating synthesis method is reported to allow the simple and green prepn. of NSC.  Particularly, small-mol. dithiooxamide can be directly converted to NSC through a facile thermal condensation process, serving as precursor, template, and self-doping agent simultaneously.  In account of its high ionic and electronic cond., increased interlayer spacing, unique layers assembled structure and efficient N, S co-doping, the NSC obtained at 800° exhibits excellent sodium storage performances, including prominent reversible capacity (316.1 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 ≤ 100 cycles), remarkable rate capability (178.3 mAh g-1 at 3 A g-1), and robust stability upon long-term cycling (213.6 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 up to 2000 cycles), rendering itself to be a promising candidate for practical sodium-ion battery.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003215"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Liquid State Templates for Constructing B, N, Co Doping Porous Carbons with a Boosting of Potassium Ion Storage Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Poly tannic acid carbon rods as anode materials for high performance lithium and sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Gang; Kong, Qingquan; Yao, Weitang; Wang, Qingyuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">629</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_A</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">832-845</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to abundant resources and low prices, biomass-derived carbons as anodes for lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been widely reported.  However, it is still a challenge to design a biomass-derived carbon material that has immunity to environmental influences, stable chem. compn. and controllable morphol.  In this paper, tannic acid (TA) as a precursor is first reported to synthesize rod structures with abundant mesopores and defects (PTA-700).  These features can provide more active sites and space for lithium and sodium ions storage, which is conducive to lithium and sodium ions transfer.  Excellent electrochem. performance is obsd. in LIBs (535 mAh/g after 100 cycles at 0.1 A/g) and SIBs (114.0 mAh/g after 3000 cycles at 1 A/g).  Kinetics anal. and d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. were carried out to further analyze the superior lithium and sodium ions storage performance of PTA-700.  More importantly, PTA-700 solves many problems faced by traditional biomass-derived carbons in commercialization.  Our work suggests an effective way to develop high-performance biomass-derived carbon anode materials for LIBs and SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.08.131"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">S Self-Doped Carbon Architectures with Heteroatoms Containing Nitrogen, Oxygen and Sulfur as High-Performance Anodes for Lithium-and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pre-oxidation of lignin precursors for hard carbon anode with boosted lithium-ion storage capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Du, Yi-Feng; Sun, Guo-Hua; Li, Yan; Cheng, Jia-Yao; Chen, Jing-Peng; Song, Ge; Kong, Qing-Qiang; Xie, Li-Jing; Chen, Cheng-Meng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">178</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">243-255</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lignin-derived hard carbon (HC) has great potential as energy storage materials.  However, it is difficult to obtain desired electrochem. performances by direct carbonization of lignin.  Herein, we demonstrate a pre-oxidn. strategy to enhance the reversible capacity of hard carbon with lignin as precursor.  The pre-oxidn. mechanism and its influence on the microstructures of the resulted hard carbon are systematically studied.  Based on in-situ FT-IR and 13C NMR spectrum, etc., it is confirmed that three dominant configurations of oxygen-contg. functional groups are formed during the process, and the content of the desired carbonyl groups (C=O) reaches a max. value at a pre-oxidn. temp. of 200°C.  Meanwhile, the alkyl groups are transformed into peroxides or alcs., contributing to intermol. cross-linkage within lignin.  As a result, the obtained material with highly random orientation nanotexture gives a much larger d002 and abundant porous structure.  Benefiting from these structural merits, the optimized lignin-derived hard carbon enables excellent Li-ion storage performance with a reversible capacity of 584 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1.  This work provides insights into the rational design of high-performance hard carbon anodes for Li-ion batteries and beyond.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000283"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cahyadi, H.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revealing the Intercalation Mechanisms of Lithium, Sodium, and Potassium in Hard Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Alvin, Stevanus; Cahyadi, Handi Setiadi; Hwang, Jieun; Chang, Wonyoung; Kwak, Sang Kyu; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000283</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries owing to its high stability, widespread availability, low-cost, and excellent performance.  Understanding the carrier-ion storage mechanism is a prerequisite for developing high-performance electrode materials; however, the underlying ion storage mechanism in hard carbon has been a topic of debate because of its complex structure.  Herein, it is demonstrated that the Li+-, Na+-, and K+-ion storage mechanisms in hard carbon are based on the adsorption of ions on the surface of active sites (e.g., deffects, edges, and residual heteroatoms) in the sloping voltage region, followed by intercalation into the graphitic layers in the low-voltage plateau region.  At a low c.d. of 3 mA g-1, the graphitic layers of hard carbon are unlocked to permit Li+-ion intercalation, resulting in a plateau region in the lithium-ion batteries.  To gain insights into the ion storage mechanism, exptl. observations including various ex situ techniques, a const.-current const.-voltage method, and diffusivity measurements are correlated with the theor. estn. of changes in carbon structures and insertion voltages during ion insertion obtained using the d. functional theory.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.01.388"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Yield Microstructure-Controlled Amorphous Carbon Anode Materials through a Pre-Oxidation Strategy for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-yield microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon anode materials through a pre-oxidation strategy for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yi; Lu, Peng; Liang, Xin; Chen, Chunhua; Xiang, Hongfa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">786</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">468-474</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the low cost and abundant resource of sodium, sodium-ion batteries demonstrate bright application prospects for large-scale energy storage systems.  Microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon with proper surface area and high electronic cond. is considered to be one of the most promising anode material.  Nevertheless, the cost of the reported carbon materials is still high because of the low carbon yield and expensive precursors.  Besides, the low initial coulombic efficiency is also a big challenge.  Herein, a high-yielding (70%) microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon is achieved via a pre-oxidn. stabilization process and following carbonization of the mixed pitch and phenol formaldehyde resin precursor.  The effects of pre-oxidn. stabilization on adjusting the microstructure of amorphous carbon are systematically investigated, as well as the electrochem. performance.  The optimal sample exhibits high initial coulombic efficiency (82%), high reversible capacity (268.3 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C) and good rate capability (106 mAh g-1 at 4 C) as an anode material of sodium-ion batteries.  This high-performance amorphous carbon material is prepd. via a controllable and low-cost strategy, presenting an appealing development of practical anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202202851"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Concave Engineering of Hollow Carbon Spheres toward Advanced Anode Material for Sodium/Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Edge-Nitrogen Enriched Porous Carbon Nanosheets Anodes with Enlarged Interlayer Distance for Fast Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Chong; Yang, Wang; Ma, Guang; Che, Sai; Li, Yun; Jia, Yan; Chen, Ni; Huang, Guoyong; Li, Yongfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2204375</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of nitrogen-doped porous carbon for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) has attracted tremendous attention.  Herein, a series of edge-nitrogen enriched porous carbon nanosheets (ENPCNs) are synthesized by annealing g-C3N4 and glucose in a sealed graphite crucible at different temps. (T = 700, 800, and 900°C).  Surprisingly, under the closed thermal treatment condition, the ENPCNs-T possess a high N-doping level (&gt;12.62 at%) and different carbon interlayer distance ranging from 0.429 to 0.487 nm.  By correlating the carbon interlayer distance with the N configurations of ENPCNs-T materials, a reasonable perception of the important influence of pyrrolic N on the increase of carbon interlayer distance is proposed.  When applied as anode materials for SIBs, the ENPCNs-800 exhibits a remarkable capacity (294.1 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate performance (132.8 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and outstanding cycle life (180.6 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles with a capacity retention of 104.7%).  Meanwhile, the characterizations of cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy demonstrate that the edge-nitrogen doping and enlarged carbon interlayer distance improve the capacity and fast charging performance of ENPCNs-800.  Considering the detailed investigation of the Na+ storage mechanism and excellent electrochem. performance of ENPCNs-800, this work can pave a new avenue for the research of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202300107"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Initiating Fluorine Chemistry in Polycyclic Aromatic Hydrocarbon Derived Carbon for New Cluster Mode Na Storage with Superhigh Capacity</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2300107</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
