                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tailoring natural anthracite carbon materials towards considerable electrochemical properties with exploration of ester/ether-based electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Yu; Yuan, Shaohui; Zhao, Wenqing; Yi, Chenxing; Zeng, Zihao; Xie, Siyan; Yang, Yue; Sun, Wei; Ji, Xiaobo; Ge, Peng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9668-9681</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon, as a promising com. material, has captured a lot of attention for use in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  But, their energy-storage mechanism is still confusing, esp. the effect of an ester/ether-based electrolyte.  Attractive because of its rich resources and low cost, natural coal has been regarded as an important candidate.  Through optimization of pyrolysis temp., a series of significant traits towards improvements in energy-storage ability were tailored, including graphitization degree, interlayer distance and hetero-atoms (oxygen, sulfur).  As an SIB anode, the optimized sample delivers a capacity of 252 mA h g-1 in an ester-based electrolyte and 325 mA h g-1 in ether-based systems.  Through detailed anal., it could be confirmed that the relatively small energy of dissoln. would induce an enhancement in adsorption behavior.  The flexible Na-solvation shells weaken the combining energy in a graphitized interlayer and compact ring-structure, resulting in improved capacity.  More significantly, with the assistance of an ether-based solvation shell, the strong force between quasi-metallic Na and carbon atoms is reduced, facilitating the stabilization of the low-voltage capacity contribution even at high c.d.  Given this, the results are anticipated to provide an in-depth understanding of Na-ion diffusion with a solvation shell, and an effective strategy for natural coal-based carbon materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref53" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.07.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Towards Enhanced Sodium Storage of Hard Carbon Anodes: Regulating the Oxygen Content in Precursor by Low-Temperature Hydrogen Reduction</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical micro-composite assembled from Bi spheres and expanded graphite flakes as anodes for sodium-ion half/full cells with excellent comprehensive electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cai, Shan; Yan, Fen; Zhao, Yanxu; Li, Mingqi; Chen, Yiwen; He, Xinrui; Wang, Chao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">430</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">132938</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing anode materials with both excellent comprehensive electrochem. performance and low cost is crit. for the large-scale practical application of sodium-ion batteries.  Herein, a novel hierarchical micro-composite assembled from Bi nano/submicron spheres and expanded graphite flakes (labeled as H-BiS/EGF) is fabricated by facile and scalable methods, using low-cost starting materials.  As anodes for sodium-ion half cells, the H-BiS/EGF micro-composite exhibits a first coulombic efficiency of 85% with a reversible capacity of around 288 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1, outstanding cycle stability (95% capacity retention for 17,300 cycles at 5 A g-1) and superior rate capability (228 mAh g-1 at 25 A g-1).  The sodium-ion full cell, which was constructed with the H-BiS/EGF anode and the synthesized C coated Na3V2(PO4)3/rGO as the cathode, delivers a high energy d. (180 Wh kg-1 at 1C) and good cycle performance (95.9% capacity retention after 600 cycles at 10C).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.138007"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Interface and Electronic Structure Dual-Engineering on Mose2 with Multi-Ion/Electron Transportation Channels for Boosted Sodium-Ion Half/Full Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                 10.1016/j.cej.2022.138007</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D450%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D138007%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BGuo%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BGuan%26author%3DX.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BZhu%26author%3DH.%2BFu%26author%3DQ.%2BLiu%26author%3DB.%2BWei%26author%3DH.%2BGeng%26title%3DInterface%2Band%2BElectronic%2BStructure%2BDual-Engineering%2Bon%2BMose2%2Bwith%2BMulti-Ion%252FElectron%2BTransportation%2BChannels%2Bfor%2BBoosted%2BSodium-Ion%2BHalf%252FFull%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2022.138007&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2022.138007&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interface and electronic structure dual-engineering on MoSe2 with multi-ion/electron transportation channels for boosted sodium-ion half/full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Jia; Yang, Jun; Guan, Jinpeng; Chen, Xinhe; Zhu, Yi; Fu, Hao; Liu, Quan; Wei, Bo; Geng, Hongbo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">450</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">138007</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is of great significance to design and prep. high performance anode materials for the development of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  In this work, the innovative approach of interface and electronic structure dual-engineering is applied on MoSe2 to fabricate novel C/N co-doped bilayer hollow structured MoSe2 nanosheets (BH-MoSe2@CNBs).  With the comparison of traditional MoSe2/C composite, the sandwich structured MoSe2 with double carbon coating can bring multi-ion/electron transportation channels, favoring the Na+ storage and charge transfer kinetics.  Specifically, the inner carbon shell as a supporting skeleton not only restrains the agglomeration of lamellar MoSe2, but also buffers the stress of sodium ions (de)insertion.  The outer carbon layer plays a crucial role in adsorbing the polyselenide intermediates, maintaining the stability and reversible capacity of the middle MoSe2 electrode.  As anode for SIBs, BH-MoSe2@CNBs exhibit 347 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 after 1300 cycles, which is comparable with the previously reported MoSe2-based electrode in SIBs.  Addnl., the BH-MoSe2@CNBs//Na3V2(PO4)2O2F full cell can reach an energy d. of 107.4 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 3832 W kg-1, indicating the potential practical application.  The theor. calcn. is also conducted to confirm the superior Na+ adsorption of BH-MoSe2@CNBs.  The interface and electronic structure dual-engineering on MoSe2 can provide innovative points for the exploitation of efficient anode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref60" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2021.04.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dimov, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, J.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okada, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin Phosphide-Carbon Composite as a High-Performance Anode Active Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Energy Density</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin phosphide-carbon composite as a high-performance anode active material for sodium-ion batteries with high energy density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hao, Zhiqiang; Dimov, Nikolay; Chang, Jeng-Kuei; Okada, Shigeto</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">64</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">463-474</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tin phosphide (Sn4P3) is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries because of its relatively large theor. capacity, appropriate Na+ alloying potential, and good cyclic stability.  Herein, the Sn4P3 embedded into a carbon matrix with good rate performance and long cycle life is reported.  The Sn4P3-C composite exhibits excellent rate performance (540 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1) and the highest reversible capacity (844 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1) among Sn4P3-based anodes reported so far.  Its reversible capacity is as high as 705 mAh g-1 even after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1.  Besides, its initial Coulomb efficiency can reach 85.6%, with the av. Coulomb efficiency exceeding 99.75% from the 3rd to 100th cycles.  Na2C6O6 is firstly used as a cathode when Sn4P3 acts as anode, and the Na-Sn4P3-C//Na2C6O6 full cell shows excellent electrochem. performance.  These results demonstrate that the Sn4P3-C composite prepd. in this work displays high-rate capability and superior cyclic performance, and thus is a potential anode for sodium ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref61" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202214429"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.                 10.1002/adma.202211461</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D35%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D2211461%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26issue%3D26%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BFeng%26author%3DX.%2BYin%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DS.%2BZhao%26author%3DC.%2BLi%26author%3DR.%2BWang%26author%3DQ.%2BA.%2BHuang%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26title%3DSingle%2BAtom%2BRegulated%2BHard%2BCarbons%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BRate%2Band%2BLow%2BTemperature%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.202211461&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref63" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1038/s41598-020-65552-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luchkin, S. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lipovskikh, S. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Katorova, N. S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Savina, A. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Abakumov, A. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevenson, K. J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solid-Electrolyte Interphase Nucleation and Growth on Carbonaceous Negative Electrodes for Li-Ion Batteries Visualized with In Situ Atomic Force Microscopy</span>. <i>Sci. Rep.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">8550</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/s41598-020-65552-6</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D8550%26journal%3DSci.%2BRep.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DS.%2BY.%2BLuchkin%26author%3DS.%2BA.%2BLipovskikh%26author%3DN.%2BS.%2BKatorova%26author%3DA.%2BA.%2BSavina%26author%3DA.%2BM.%2BAbakumov%26author%3DK.%2BJ.%2BStevenson%26title%3DSolid-Electrolyte%2BInterphase%2BNucleation%2Band%2BGrowth%2Bon%2BCarbonaceous%2BNegative%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BLi-Ion%2BBatteries%2BVisualized%2Bwith%2BIn%2BSitu%2BAtomic%2BForce%2BMicroscopy%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fs41598-020-65552-6&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fs41598-020-65552-6&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit63R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">63</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solid-electrolyte interphase nucleation and growth on carbonaceous negative electrodes for Li-ion batteries visualized with in situ atomic force microscopy</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luchkin, Sergey Yu.; Lipovskikh, Svetlana A.; Katorova, Natalia S.; Savina, Aleksandra A.; Abakumov, Artem M.; Stevenson, Keith J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8550</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SRCEC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2045-2322</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Abstr.: Li-ion battery performance and life cycle strongly depend on a passivation layer called solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI).  Its structure and compn. are studied in great details, while its formation process remains elusive due to difficulty of in situ measurements of battery electrodes.  Here we provide a facile methodol. for in situ at. force microscopy (AFM) measurements of SEI formation on cross-sectioned composite battery electrodes allowing for direct observations of SEI formation on various types of carbonaceous neg. electrode materials for Li-ion batteries.  Using this approach, we obsd. SEI nucleation and growth on highly oriented pyrolytic graphite (HOPG), MesoCarbon MicroBeads (MCMB) graphite, and non-graphitizable amorphous carbon (hard carbon).  Besides the details of the formation mechanism, the elec. and mech. properties of the SEI layers were assessed.  The comparative observations revealed that the electrode potentials for SEI formation differ depending on the nature of the electrode material, whereas the adhesion of SEI to the electrode surface clearly correlates with the surface roughness of the electrode.  Finally, the same approach applied to a pos. LiNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 electrode did not reveal any signature of cathodic SEI thus demonstrating fundamental differences in the stabilization mechanisms of the neg. and pos. electrodes in Li-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref64"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref64" class="refNumLink">64</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit64"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">GENG, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">WANG, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">LIANG, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt-Manganese Co-Doped Metal-Organic Framework Compound Activates Peroxymonosulfate for Tetracycline Degradation[J]</span>. <i>China Powder Sci. Technol.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">113</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">122</span></span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D30%26publication_year%3D2024%26pages%3D113-122%26journal%3DChina%2BPowder%2BSci.%2BTechnol.%26issue%3D2%26author%3DS.%2BGENG%26author%3DH.%2BWANG%26author%3DF.%2BLIANG%26title%3DCobalt-Manganese%2BCo-Doped%2BMetal-Organic%2BFramework%2BCompound%2BActivates%2BPeroxymonosulfate%2Bfor%2BTetracycline%2BDegradation%255BJ%255D&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c03425&amp;doiOfLink=&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" (g) Theoretical simulations of the adsorption of Na<sup>+</sup> on C-vacancies, C-vacancies and 1 (C═O), C-vacancies and 2 (C═O), and C-vacancies and 3 (C═O), with the corresponding adsorption energies (<i>E</i><sub>ad</sub>).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/large/am4c03425_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c03425&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><figure data-id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><a class="internalNav" aria-label="scroll to figure" href="#fig4"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/medium/am4c03425_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c03425/asset/images/large/am4c03425_0004.jpeg" id="rightTab-gr4" class="rightTab-fig internalNav"></a><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Charge/discharge profiles at 0.05 A g<sup>–1</sup> and ex-situ <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> values from Raman spectroscopy under various stages in (a) DEGDME- and (b) EC/DEC-based electrolytes. (b, c) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients calculated from the GITT potential profiles for discharge processes (panel (b)) and charge processes (panel (c)). (d) Nyquist plots.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Layer-structured SnSSe attracts much attention as an anode material for potassium storage due to its large theor. capacity.  Unfortunately, their practical application is severely restrained by the dramatic volumetric variation of SnSSe.  Herein, we synthesize ultrafine SnSSe/multilayer graphene nanosheet (SnSSe/MGS) by a vacuum solid-phase reaction and subsequent ball milling.  Owing to the strong synergistic effect between the two components, the obtained SnSSe/MGS nanocomposite exhibits a high reversible capacity (423 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1), excellent rate property (218 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and stable cycling performance (271 mAh g-1 after 500 cycles at 100 mA g-1) in potassium-ion half batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The overall electrochem. performance of carbon anodes for potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) is considerably restricted by their poor cyclic property and rate capability issues.  Herein, we report a water chestnut-derived slope-dominated carbon anode through moderate-temp. pyrolysis at 900°C, which manifests a high initial reversible capacity of 253.2 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, remarkable rate property of 134.8 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1, and impressive cycling performance of 220.5 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 1000 cycles. The improved potassium storage properties could be ascribed to the disordered microstructure with relatively larger oxygen-contg. defect concn., high sp. surface area, and stochastically oriented short graphene nanosheets.  D. functional theory calcns. illustrate that oxygen doping can effectively alter the charge d. distribution of carbon and facilitate the adsorption of K+ on water chestnut-derived carbon, which boosts potassium ion storage.  This work would provide a promising avenue to design and synthesize slope-dominated carbon materials for low-cost PIBs with excellent rate and cycling properties and high safety.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202207751"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Terrones, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Combustion Activation Induced Solid-State Synthesis for N, B Co-Doped Carbon/Zinc Borate Anode with a Boosting of Sodium Storage Performance</span>. <i>Adv.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbons have shown considerable promise as anodes for emerging sodium-ion battery technologies.  Current understanding of sodium-storage behavior in hard carbons attributes capacity to filling of graphitic interlayers and pores, and adsorption at defects, although there is still considerable debate regarding the voltages at which these mechanisms occur.  Here, ex situ23Na solid-state NMR and total scattering studies on a systematically tuned series of hard carbons revealed the formation of increasingly metallic sodium clusters in direct correlation to the growing pore size, occurring only in samples which exhibited a low voltage plateau.  Combining exptl. results with DFT calcns., we propose a revised mechanistic model in which sodium ions store first simultaneously and continuously at defects, within interlayers and on pore surfaces.  Once these higher energy binding sites are filled, pore filling occurs during the plateau region, where the densely confined sodium takes on a greater degree of metallicity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding of the Sodium Storage Mechanism in Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Carbon Energy.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">1133</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1150</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbon has been regarded as the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its low cost, high reversible capacity, and low working potential.  However, the uncertain sodium storage mechanism hinders the rational design and synthesis of high-performance hard carbon anode materials for practical SIBs.  During the past decades, tremendous efforts have been put to stimulate the development of hard carbon materials.  In this review, we discuss the recent progress of the study on the sodium storage mechanism of hard carbon anodes, and the effective strategies to improve their sodium storage performance have been summarized.  It is anticipated that hard carbon anodes with high electrochem. properties will be inspired and fabricated for large-scale energy storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.2210203119"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Step-By-Step Desolvation Enables High-Rate And Ultra-Stable Sodium Storage in Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Proc.                         rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Elucidating the Mechanism of Fast Na Storage Kinetics in Ether Electrolytes for Hard Carbon Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Ruiqi; Zheng, Lumin; Bai, Ying; Ni, Qiao; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng; Ren, Haixia; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium storage performance of a hard carbon (HC) anode in ether electrolytes exhibits a higher initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) and better rate performance compared to conventional ester electrolytes.  However, the mechanism behind faster Na storage kinetics for HC in ether electrolytes remains unclear.  Herein, a unique solvated Na+ and Na+ co-intercalation mechanism in ether electrolytes is reported using designed monodispersed HC nanospheres.  In addn., a thin solid electrolyte interphase film with a high inorg. proportion formed in an ether electrolyte is visualized by cryo transmission electron microscopy and depth-profiling XPS, which facilitates Na+ transportation, and results in a high ICE.  Furthermore, the fast solvated Na+ diffusion kinetics in ether electrolytes are also revealed via mol. dynamics simulation.  Owing to the contribution of the ether electrolytes, an excellent rate performance (214 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 with an ultrahigh plateau capacity of 120 mAh g-1) and a high ICE (84.93% at 1 A g-1) are obsd. in a half cell; in a full cell, an attractive specific capacity of 110.3 mAh g-1 is achieved after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.10.049"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailored Edge-Heteroatom Tri-Doping Strategy of Turbostratic Carbon Anodes for High-Rate Performance Lithium and Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>54</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">498</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">507</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The overall performance of carbon-based materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is still restricted by the sluggish transfer kinetics of Na+ and limited rate capability.  Specifically, introducing ultramicropores (pores width &lt;0.7 nm) into carbon materials may be effective in improving the anode performance of SIBs.  However, due to the difficulty of their synthesis and homogeneity regulation, ultramicroporous carbon as advanced SIB anodes as well as their sodium storage mechanisms have seldom been investigated.  Herein, carbon spheres with centralized ultramicropores and abundant C=O is facilely obtained by combining the in situ ion activation and the novel quant. air-assisted carbonization process for the first time.  The quant. air acts not only as a mild agent to activate the materials, but also as an oxygen dopant for forming oxygen-contg. functional groups.  As the optimized anode, quant. air-assisted carbonized spheres with a precursor wt. of 0.3 g (QACS-0.3) delivers a high rate capability (265 and 121 mAh g-1 at 0.05 and 5.0 A g-1, resp.) and good cycling stability (126 mAh g-1 after 5000 cycles at 5.0 A g-1).  Kinetic anal., theor. calcn., and ex situ testing technologies reveal that the ultramicropores can facilitate the diffusion of Na+ below 0.2 V; the synergistic effect of defects, C=O, and ultramicropores can extend the discharge curves and effectively improve the adsorption capacity of carbon materials.  Addnl., a new discharge model is proposed to explain the sodium storage behaviors in these electrodes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref17" class="rightTabRefNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202100808"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Egun, I. Nevertheless, com. porous carbon materials have some disadvantages such as high prodn. cost, corrosion of equipment, and emission of toxic gases and byproduct pollutants during prodn.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Natural materials have always attracted intensive attention from multidisciplinary scientists all over the world.  In fact, the ingenious and reasonable synthetic strategies of the limited components can always make natural materials achieve a superior performance that is far beyond their own.  Meanwhile, the local properties can det. the overall performance through regulating multiple characteristics, including structure, compn., and interface.  Living organisms can inspire the fabrication of artificial materials, which provides a clear vision for advanced materials research.  Therefore, inspired by this strategy, biomimetic structural materials are used to meet the strict and even extreme requirements of engineering materials.  In this review, we mainly clarify the difference of local properties in natural materials and explain how living organisms utilize very limited elements and compds. to control the local properties and further realize some specific function to adapt to the specific requirement of the environment.  In addn., the manufg. technologies and strategies common to bio-inspired structural materials are summarized.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Bioinspired mineralization is a powerful method for designing and prepg. nanomaterials.  In this work, we developed a bioinspired mineralization approach under freezing conditions and fabricated Me cellulose (MC)/NaHCO3 flake precursors with a sophisticated hierarchical structure.  Based on this, amazing wing-like porous carbon sheets (WPCSs) assembled by numerous interconnected hollow carbon bubbles were obtained after carbonization and removal of inorg. crystals, which are seldom obtained by other artificial methods.  Benefiting from their open framework, large surface area, and enlarged interlayer spacing of graphitized nanocrystallites, the obtained WPCSs exhibited an obvious boost in potassium storage performance.  As an anode of potassium-ion batteries, they showed high reversible capacities of 347 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and 122 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 and relatively stable cyclability for 3000 cycles.  The assembled WPCS//WPCS potassium-ion hybrid supercapacitor delivered a high energy d. of 108 Wh kg-1 at a power d. of 280 W kg-1.                         rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rice husk-derived hard carbons as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Liu, Yuhan; Fang, Yuyan; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">127</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">658-666</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn ever-increasing attention for scalable elec. energy storage owing to the inexhaustible sources and wide distribution of sodium.  However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.  This work could intensify the fundamental understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in biomass-derived hard carbons.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1039/D1CS00948F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ether-Based Electrolytes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>51</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">11</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">4484</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4536</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1CS00948F</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ether-based electrolytes for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Ying; Wu, Feng; Li, Yu; Liu, Mingquan; Feng, Xin; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4484-4536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be strong candidates for large-scale energy storage with the benefits of cost-effectiveness and sodium abundance.  Reliable electrolytes, as ionic conductors that regulate the electrochem. reaction behavior and the nature of the interface and electrode, are indispensable in the development of advanced SIBs with high Coulombic efficiency, stable cycling performance and high rate capability.  Conventional carbonate-based electrolytes encounter numerous obstacles for their wide application in SIBs due to the formation of a dissolvable, continuous-thickening solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layer and inferior stability with electrodes.  Comparatively, ether-based electrolytes (EBEs) are emerging in the secondary battery field with fascinating properties to improve the performance of batteries, esp. SIBs.  Their stable solvation structure enables highly reversible solvent-co-intercalation reactions and the formation of a thin and stable SEI.  However, although EBEs can provide more stable cycling and rapid sodiation kinetics in electrodes, benefitting from their favorable electrolyte/electrode interactions such as chem. compatibility and good wettability, their special chem. is still being investigated and puzzling.  In this review, we provide a thorough and comprehensive overview on the developmental history, fundamental characteristics, superiorities and mechanisms of EBEs, together with their advances in other battery systems.  Notably, the relation among electrolyte science, interfacial chem. and electrochem. performance is highlighted, which is of great significance for the in-depth understanding of battery chem.  Finally, future perspectives and potential directions are proposed to navigate the design and optimization of electrolytes and electrolyte/electrode interfaces for advanced batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202209523"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Unraveling the Mechanism of Different Kinetics Performance Between Ether and Carbonate Ester Electrolytes in Hard Carbon Electrode</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">48</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2209523</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.202209523</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling mechanism of different kinetics performance between ether and carbonate ester electrolytes in hard carbon electrode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yi, Xiaoli; Li, Xinhai; Zhong, Jing; Wang, Siwu; Wang, Zhixing; Guo, Huajun; Wang, Jiexi; Yan, Guochun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">32</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2209523</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ether electrolytes exhibit better rate kinetics than carbonate ester electrolytes when used in several kinds of anode materials, esp. in hard carbon (HC) for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the mechanism causing the remarkable kinetics difference is still unclear.  Here, a three-electrode system is used first to eliminate the influence of polarization from the Na counter electrode.  Then, there is systematic exploration from three steps of the electrode reaction process (Na+) storage in HC; de-solvation; Na+ migration through solid electrolyte interphase (SE), and the underlying mysteries are uncovered.  For Na+ storage in the bulk of the HC, it is found that two systems show the same storage mechanism and Na metallic nanoparticles will appear when discharged to 0.1 V.  In addn., faster de-solvation of the ether electrolyte is uncovered by three-electrode temp.-dependent EIS and solvation free energies calcn.  Moreover, the difference of the SEI layers is unraveled by XPS etching, SEM, and differential electrochem. mass spectrometry.  Most importantly, by discriminating the impacts of the SEI layers and de-solvation behavior, it can be concluded that the de-solvation process is the rate-controlling step of the electrode reaction process and is the main factor causing the kinetics differences between the two electrolytes.  The research provides a clear mechanism to illuminate fast kinetics for ether electrolytes, which will promote its application in SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA00845E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting the Ultrahigh Initial Coulombic Efficiency of Porous Carbon Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries Via in Situ Fabrication of a Passivation Interface</span>. <i>J.                         rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting the ultrahigh initial coulombic efficiency of porous carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries via in situ fabrication of a passivation interface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Minghao; Li, Yu; Wu, Feng; Wang, Zhaohua; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous carbon materials are regarded as one of the most promising candidates for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to their fast sodium storage performance.  However, the inadequate initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) resulting from the large sp. surface area still hinders the commercialization of porous carbon anodes.  Thus, it is important to synthesize porous carbon anodes with high electrochem. performance and improved ICE.  Here we prep. a nitrogen and oxygen rich porous carbon material (NOPC) and construct a uniform passivation layer using a sodium CM-cellulose (CMC) binder on the surface of the NOPC material.  The uniform passivation layer effectively deactivates the functional groups and suppresses the decompn. of electrolytes, resulting in an excellent ICE of 90%, which is ultrahigh and competitive among the reported carbon-based anodes in SIBs.  Specifically, the as-prepd. porous carbon anode delivers a reversible capacity of 191.7 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 90%.  This work suggests a general method to improve the ICE of a carbon material and hopefully facilitates the commercialization process of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202100538"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mathur, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vitreum Etching Assisted Fabrication of Porous Hollow Carbon Architectures for Enhanced Capacitive Sodium and Potassium Ion Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">25</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2100538</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen and sulfur co-doping is emerging as a promising approach to prominently improve the sodium storage performance of carbonaceous materials.  However, poisonous chems. and rigorous conditions are normally involved in their prepn., esp. in the sulfidation process.  Therefore, developing novel, facile and eco-friendly approaches to construct nitrogen and sulfur co-doped carbon (NSC) is still challenging.  In this work, a facile self-templating synthesis method is reported to allow the simple and green prepn. of NSC.  Particularly, small-mol. dithiooxamide can be directly converted to NSC through a facile thermal condensation process, serving as precursor, template, and self-doping agent simultaneously.  In account of its high ionic and electronic cond., increased interlayer spacing, unique layers assembled structure and efficient N, S co-doping, the NSC obtained at 800° exhibits excellent sodium storage performances, including prominent reversible capacity (316.1 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 ≤ 100 cycles), remarkable rate capability (178.3 mAh g-1 at 3 A g-1), and robust stability upon long-term cycling (213.6 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 up to 2000 cycles), rendering itself to be a promising candidate for practical sodium-ion battery.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202003215"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Liquid State Templates for Constructing B, N, Co Doping Porous Carbons with a Boosting of Potassium Ion Storage Performance</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pre-oxidation of lignin precursors for hard carbon anode with boosted lithium-ion storage capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Du, Yi-Feng; Sun, Guo-Hua; Li, Yan; Cheng, Jia-Yao; Chen, Jing-Peng; Song, Ge; Kong, Qing-Qiang; Xie, Li-Jing; Chen, Cheng-Meng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">178</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">243-255</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Lignin-derived hard carbon (HC) has great potential as energy storage materials.  However, it is difficult to obtain desired electrochem. performances by direct carbonization of lignin.  Herein, we demonstrate a pre-oxidn. strategy to enhance the reversible capacity of hard carbon with lignin as precursor.  The pre-oxidn. mechanism and its influence on the microstructures of the resulted hard carbon are systematically studied.  Based on in-situ FT-IR and 13C NMR spectrum, etc., it is confirmed that three dominant configurations of oxygen-contg. functional groups are formed during the process, and the content of the desired carbonyl groups (C=O) reaches a max. value at a pre-oxidn. temp. of 200°C.  Meanwhile, the alkyl groups are transformed into peroxides or alcs., contributing to intermol. cross-linkage within lignin.  As a result, the obtained material with highly random orientation nanotexture gives a much larger d002 and abundant porous structure.  Benefiting from these structural merits, the optimized lignin-derived hard carbon enables excellent Li-ion storage performance with a reversible capacity of 584 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1.  This work provides insights into the rational design of high-performance hard carbon anodes for Li-ion batteries and beyond.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202000283"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Alvin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cahyadi, H.                 10.1002/aenm.202000283</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revealing the Intercalation Mechanisms of Lithium, Sodium, and Potassium in Hard Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Alvin, Stevanus; Cahyadi, Handi Setiadi; Hwang, Jieun; Chang, Wonyoung; Kwak, Sang Kyu; Kim, Jaehoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000283</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries and potassium-ion batteries owing to its high stability, widespread availability, low-cost, and excellent performance.  Understanding the carrier-ion storage mechanism is a prerequisite for developing high-performance electrode materials; however, the underlying ion storage mechanism in hard carbon has been a topic of debate because of its complex structure.  Herein, it is demonstrated that the Li+-, Na+-, and K+-ion storage mechanisms in hard carbon are based on the adsorption of ions on the surface of active sites (e.g., deffects, edges, and residual heteroatoms) in the sloping voltage region, followed by intercalation into the graphitic layers in the low-voltage plateau region.  At a low c.d. of 3 mA g-1, the graphitic layers of hard carbon are unlocked to permit Li+-ion intercalation, resulting in a plateau region in the lithium-ion batteries.  To gain insights into the ion storage mechanism, exptl. observations including various ex situ techniques, a const.-current const.-voltage method, and diffusivity measurements are correlated with the theor. estn. of changes in carbon structures and insertion voltages during ion insertion obtained using the d. functional theory.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.01.388"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Yield Microstructure-Controlled Amorphous Carbon Anode Materials through a Pre-Oxidation Strategy for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.01.388</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-yield microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon anode materials through a pre-oxidation strategy for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yi; Lu, Peng; Liang, Xin; Chen, Chunhua; Xiang, Hongfa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to the low cost and abundant resource of sodium, sodium-ion batteries demonstrate bright application prospects for large-scale energy storage systems.  Microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon with proper surface area and high electronic cond. is considered to be one of the most promising anode material.  Nevertheless, the cost of the reported carbon materials is still high because of the low carbon yield and expensive precursors.  Besides, the low initial coulombic efficiency is also a big challenge.  Herein, a high-yielding (70%) microstructure-controlled amorphous carbon is achieved via a pre-oxidn. stabilization process and following carbonization of the mixed pitch and phenol formaldehyde resin precursor.  The effects of pre-oxidn. stabilization on adjusting the microstructure of amorphous carbon are systematically investigated, as well as the electrochem. performance.  The optimal sample exhibits high initial coulombic efficiency (82%), high reversible capacity (268.3 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C) and good rate capability (106 mAh g-1 at 4 C) as an anode material of sodium-ion batteries.  This high-performance amorphous carbon material is prepd. via a controllable and low-cost strategy, presenting an appealing development of practical anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202202851"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Concave Engineering of Hollow Carbon Spheres toward Advanced Anode Material for Sodium/Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Edge-Nitrogen Enriched Porous Carbon Nanosheets Anodes with Enlarged Interlayer Distance for Fast Charging Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Chong; Yang, Wang; Ma, Guang; Che, Sai; Li, Yun; Jia, Yan; Chen, Ni; Huang, Guoyong; Li, Yongfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of nitrogen-doped porous carbon for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) has attracted tremendous attention.  Herein, a series of edge-nitrogen enriched porous carbon nanosheets (ENPCNs) are synthesized by annealing g-C3N4 and glucose in a sealed graphite crucible at different temps. (T = 700, 800, and 900°C).  Surprisingly, under the closed thermal treatment condition, the ENPCNs-T possess a high N-doping level (&gt;12.62 at%) and different carbon interlayer distance ranging from 0.429 to 0.487 nm.  By correlating the carbon interlayer distance with the N configurations of ENPCNs-T materials, a reasonable perception of the important influence of pyrrolic N on the increase of carbon interlayer distance is proposed.  When applied as anode materials for SIBs, the ENPCNs-800 exhibits a remarkable capacity (294.1 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate performance (132.8 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1), and outstanding cycle life (180.6 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles with a capacity retention of 104.7%).  Meanwhile, the characterizations of cyclic voltammetry, galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy demonstrate that the edge-nitrogen doping and enlarged carbon interlayer distance improve the capacity and fast charging performance of ENPCNs-800.  Considering the detailed investigation of the Na+ storage mechanism and excellent electrochem. performance of ENPCNs-800, this work can pave a new avenue for the research of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref49" class="rightTabRefNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit49" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202300107"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Initiating Fluorine Chemistry in Polycyclic Aromatic Hydrocarbon Derived Carbon for New Cluster Mode Na Storage with Superhigh Capacity</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">22</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2300107</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9668-9681</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon, as a promising com. material, has captured a lot of attention for use in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  But, their energy-storage mechanism is still confusing, esp. the effect of an ester/ether-based electrolyte.  Attractive because of its rich resources and low cost, natural coal has been regarded as an important candidate.  Through optimization of pyrolysis temp., a series of significant traits towards improvements in energy-storage ability were tailored, including graphitization degree, interlayer distance and hetero-atoms (oxygen, sulfur).  As an SIB anode, the optimized sample delivers a capacity of 252 mA h g-1 in an ester-based electrolyte and 325 mA h g-1 in ether-based systems.  Through detailed anal., it could be confirmed that the relatively small energy of dissoln. would induce an enhancement in adsorption behavior.  The flexible Na-solvation shells weaken the combining energy in a graphitized interlayer and compact ring-structure, resulting in improved capacity.  More significantly, with the assistance of an ether-based solvation shell, the strong force between quasi-metallic Na and carbon atoms is reduced, facilitating the stabilization of the low-voltage capacity contribution even at high c.d.  Given this, the results are anticipated to provide an in-depth understanding of Na-ion diffusion with a solvation shell, and an effective strategy for natural coal-based carbon materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref53" class="rightTabRefNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.07.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Towards Enhanced Sodium Storage of Hard Carbon Anodes: Regulating the Oxygen Content in Precursor by Low-Temperature Hydrogen Reduction</span>. <i>Energy Environ.
